{"uri": "2024-07-433775725", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "21:40:50", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T21:40:50Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T21:25:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8823529481887817, "url": "https://omaha.com/swanson-usa-olympics-soccer-women-roundup/article_6efa1b05-25f7-5a59-bc4f-523f9c73c61c.html", "title": "US women off to strong start", "body": "ASSOCIATED PRESS\n\nNICE, France -- Mallory Swanson scored a pair of goals just moments apart in the first half and the United States opened the Olympics with a 3-0 victory Thursday night over Zambia, giving new coach Emma Hayes a win in her first major tournament with the team.\n\nTrinity Rodman also scored for the United States, which is looking to add a record fifth gold medal to its Olympic collection.\n\nZambia was hurt in the 33rd minute when Pauline Zulu was sent off with a red card and the team was limited to 10 players the rest of the way.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.", "source": {"uri": "omaha.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Omaha.com"}, "authors": [{"uri": {"uri": "8243744631", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "22:11:01", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T22:11:01Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T22:06:02Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8745098114013672, "url": "https://japantoday.com/category/paris-2024-olympics/canada-wins-2-1-over-new-zealand-to-open-the-olympics-after-drone-scandal-spain-beats-japan-2-1", "title": "Canada beats NZ 2-1 in women's soccer after drone scandal; Spain edges Japan 2-1", "body": "Evelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a 2-1 victory over New Zealand on Thursday in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nNew Zealand announced a day before the match that captain Ali Riley could not play in the Olympics because of an unspecified injury.\n\nJayde Riviere of Canada was ruled unavailable earlier Thursday because of an ankle injury. Shelina Zadorsky replaced her on the roster for the match.\n\nThe Ferns, playing under interim coach Michael Mayne, were making their fifth straight Olympic appearance. New Zealand's coach, Jitka Klimkova, decided to step aside for the Olympics in late June after an independent workplace employment investigation.\n\nKlimkova was cleared in the investigation, but she did not feel there was enough time to heal the environment before the tournament.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nU.S. 3, Zambia 0\n\nMallory Swanson scored a pair of goals just moments apart in the first half and the United States opened the Olympics with a 3-0 victory over Zambia on Thursday night, giving new coach Emma Hayes a win in her first major tournament with the team.\n\nTrinity Rodman also scored for the United States, which is looking to add a record fifth gold medal to its Olympic collection.\n\nZambia was hurt in the 33rd minute when Pauline Zulu was sent off with a red card and the team was limited to 10 players the rest of the way. Zulu sobbed as she left the field.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, she had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nFrance 3, Colombia 2\n\nFrance built a 3-0 lead in the first half and held off Colombia in Lyon.\n\nMarie-Antoinette Katoto scored a pair of goals and Kenza Dali added another for the hosts in Group A.\n\nCatalina Usme converted on a penalty early in the second half for Colombia, which was returning to the Olympics after missing out on the Tokyo Games. Manuela Pavi helped close the gap further with another goal in the 64th.\n\n\u00a9 Copyright 2024 The Associated Press. All rights reserved. She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nAP Soccer Writer James Robson, in Marseille, France, contributed to this report.\n\nAP Summer Olympics: https://apnews.com/hub/2024-paris-olympic-games", "source": {"uri": "register-herald.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Beckley Register-Herald"}, "authors": [{"uri": "anne_m_peterson@register-herald.com", "name": "Anne M. Zulu sobbed as she left the field.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, she had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nFrance 3, Colombia 2\n\nFrance built a 3-0 lead in the first half and held off Colombia in Lyon.\n\nMarie-Antoinette Katoto scored a pair of goals and Kenza Dali added another for the hosts in Group A.\n\nCatalina Usme converted on a penalty early in the second half for Colombia, which was returning to the Olympics after missing out on the Tokyo Games. Manuela Pavi helped close the gap further with another goal in the 64th.\n\n___\n\nAP Soccer Writer James Robson, in Marseille, France, contributed to this report.\n\n___\n\nAP Summer Olympics: https://apnews.com/hub/2024-paris-olympic-games", "source": {"uri": "seattletimes.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "The Seattle Times"}, "authors": [{"uri": "anne_m_peterson@seattletimes.com", "name": "Anne M. {"uri": "2024-07-433800952", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "22:26:21", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T22:26:21Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T22:11:34Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8588235378265381, "url": "https://www.beaumontenterprise.com/sports/article/canada-wins-2-1-over-new-zealand-to-open-the-19596725.php", "title": "Swanson's 2 goals lead US over Zambia at the Olympics, Canada tops New Zealand after drone scandal", "body": "NICE, France (AP) -- Mallory Swanson scored a pair of goals just moments apart in the first half and the United States opened the Olympics with a 3-0 victory over Zambia on Thursday night, giving new coach Emma Hayes a win in her first major tournament with the team.\n\nTrinity Rodman also scored for the United States, which is looking to add a record fifth gold medal to its Olympic collection.\n\nZambia was hurt in the 33rd minute when Pauline Zulu was sent off with a red card and the team was limited to 10 players the rest of the way. Zulu sobbed as she left the field.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\n\"If you had asked me at the beginning of the game, 'Would you be happy with a 3-nil win?' I probably would have said no,\" Hayes said. \"However, after the performance and the chances created and finding the back of the net we did, I don't want to be too hard on the girls.\"\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nSwanson called it just a start.\n\n\"I think there's little things within that game, within the play, that we need to fine-tune, that we can just keep on growing with,\" Swanson said. \"So I think there's definitely those little things, and we'll address them and fix them and keep moving forward.\"\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\n\"A lot of credit to Zambia's goalkeeper tonight, because in the first half I think we had a sequence of like six shots in a row that she saved or went off the post,\" Horan said. \"And sometimes that how it goes. I was really happy it wasn't one of those days where the ball just doesn't go in the back of the net.\"\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through the U.S. defense, which was stout throughout the match.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, she had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nThe United States will next face Germany on Sunday in Marseille.\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nFrance built a 3-0 lead in the first half and held off Colombia in Lyon.\n\nMarie-Antoinette Katoto scored a pair of goals and Kenza Dali added another for the hosts in Group A.\n\nCatalina Usme converted on a penalty early in the second half for Colombia, which was returning to the Olympics after missing out on the Tokyo Games. Manuela Pavi helped close the gap further with another goal in the 64th.\n\n___\n\nAP Soccer Writer James Robson, in Marseille, France, contributed to this report.", "source": {"uri": "beaumontenterprise.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Beaumont Enterprise"}, "authors": [{"uri": "anne_m_peterson@beaumontenterprise.com", "name": "Anne M. Zulu sobbed as she left the field.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\n\"If you had asked me at the beginning of the game, 'Would you be happy with a 3-nil win?' I probably would have said no,\" Hayes said. \"However, after the performance and the chances created and finding the back of the net we did, I don't want to be too hard on the girls.\"\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nSwanson called it just a start.\n\n\"I think there's little things within that game, within the play, that we need to fine-tune, that we can just keep on growing with,\" Swanson said. \"So I think there's definitely those little things, and we'll address them and fix them and keep moving forward.\"\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\n\"A lot of credit to Zambia's goalkeeper tonight, because in the first half I think we had a sequence of like six shots in a row that she saved or went off the post,\" Horan said. \"And sometimes that how it goes. I was really happy it wasn't one of those days where the ball just doesn't go in the back of the net.\"\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through the U.S. defense, which was stout throughout the match.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, she had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nThe United States will next face Germany on Sunday in Marseille.\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nFrance built a 3-0 lead in the first half and held off Colombia in Lyon.\n\nMarie-Antoinette Katoto scored a pair of goals and Kenza Dali added another for the hosts in Group A.\n\nCatalina Usme converted on a penalty early in the second half for Colombia, which was returning to the Olympics after missing out on the Tokyo Games. {"uri": "8243834854", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-26", "time": "00:08:27", "dateTime": "2024-07-26T00:08:27Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-26T00:07:09Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8549019694328308, "url": "https://www.eagletribune.com/swansons-2-goals-lead-us-over-zambia-at-the-olympics-canada-tops-new-zealand-after/article_5f64e05a-d636-58e7-bcb5-e8e376dc671a.html", "title": "Swanson's 2 goals lead US over Zambia at the Olympics, Canada tops New Zealand after drone scandal", "body": "Zambia's Pauline Zulu, left, walks with teammate Hellen Chanda after she was given a red card by referee Ramon Abatti, of Brazil, during a women's group B match between the United States and Zambia at Nice Stadium at the 2024 Summer Olympics, Thursday, July 25, 2024, in Nice, France.\n\nNICE, France (AP) -- Mallory Swanson scored a pair of goals just moments apart in the first half and the United States opened the Olympics with a 3-0 victory over Zambia on Thursday night, giving new coach Emma Hayes a win in her first major tournament with the team.\n\nTrinity Rodman also scored for the United States, which is looking to add a record fifth gold medal to its Olympic collection.\n\nZambia was hurt in the 33rd minute when Pauline Zulu was sent off with a red card and the team was limited to 10 players the rest of the way. Zulu sobbed as she left the field.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\n\"If you had asked me at the beginning of the game, 'Would you be happy with a 3-nil win?' I probably would have said no,\" Hayes said. \"However, after the performance and the chances created and finding the back of the net we did, I don't want to be too hard on the girls.\"\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nSwanson called it just a start.\n\n\"I think there's little things within that game, within the play, that we need to fine-tune, that we can just keep on growing with,\" Swanson said. \"So I think there's definitely those little things, and we'll address them and fix them and keep moving forward.\"\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\n\"A lot of credit to Zambia's goalkeeper tonight, because in the first half I think we had a sequence of like six shots in a row that she saved or went off the post,\" Horan said. \"And sometimes that how it goes. I was really happy it wasn't one of those days where the ball just doesn't go in the back of the net.\"\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through the U.S. defense, which was stout throughout the match.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, she had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nThe United States will next face Germany on Sunday in Marseille.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nFrance 3, Colombia 2\n\nFrance built a 3-0 lead in the first half and held off Colombia in Lyon.\n\nMarie-Antoinette Katoto scored a pair of goals and Kenza Dali added another for the hosts in Group A.\n\nCatalina Usme converted on a penalty early in the second half for Colombia, which was returning to the Olympics after missing out on the Tokyo Games. Manuela Pavi helped close the gap further with another goal in the 64th.\n\nAP Soccer Writer James Robson, in Marseille, France, contributed to this report.\n\nAP Summer Olympics: https://apnews.com/hub/2024-paris-olympic-games", "source": {"uri": "eagletribune.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Eagle-Tribune"}, "authors": [{"uri": "anne_m_peterson@eagletribune.com", "name": "Anne M. {"uri": "8243746901", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "22:09:54", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T22:09:54Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T22:09:06Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.843137264251709, "url": "https://www.oregonlive.com/soccer/2024/07/mallory-swansons-2-goals-lead-us-over-zambia-at-the-olympics.html", "title": "Mallory Swanson's 2 goals lead U.S. over Zambia at the Olympics", "body": "NICE, France -- Mallory Swanson scored a pair of goals just moments apart in the first half and the United States opened the Olympics with a 3-0 victory Thursday night over Zambia, giving new coach Emma Hayes a win in her first major tournament with the team.\n\nTrinity Rodman also scored for the United States, which is looking to add a record fifth gold medal to its Olympic collection.\n\nZambia was hurt in the 33rd minute when Pauline Zulu was sent off with a red card and the team was limited to 10 players the rest of the way.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward and Portland Thorns star Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\n-- Anne M. Peterson | AP Soccer Writer\n\n-- AP Soccer Writer James Robson, in Marseille, France, contributed to this report.", "source": {"uri": "oregonlive.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Oregon Live"}, Zulu sobbed as she left the field.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, she had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nFrance built a 3-0 lead in the first half and held off Colombia in Lyon.\n\nMarie-Antoinette Katoto scored a pair of goals and Kenza Dali added another for the hosts in Group A.\n\nCatalina Usme converted on a penalty early in the second half for Colombia, which was returning to the Olympics after missing out on the Tokyo Games. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nNew Zealand announced a day before the match that captain Ali Riley could not play in the Olympics because of an unspecified injury.\n\nJayde Riviere of Canada was ruled unavailable earlier Thursday because of an ankle injury. Shelina Zadorsky replaced her on the roster for the match.\n\nThe Ferns, playing under interim coach Michael Mayne, were making their fifth straight Olympic appearance. New Zealand's coach, Jitka Klimkova, decided to step aside for the Olympics in late June after an independent workplace employment investigation.\n\nKlimkova was cleared in the investigation, but she did not feel there was enough time to heal the environment before the tournament.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nNigeria advanced to the knockout round at last year's Women's World Cup.\n\nAP Soccer Writer James Robson, in Marseille, France, contributed to this report.\n\nAP Summer Olympics: https://apnews.com/hub/2024-paris-olympic-games", "source": {"uri": "register-herald.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Beckley Register-Herald"}, "authors": [{"uri": "anne_m_peterson@register-herald.com", "name": "Anne M. She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nPeople are also reading...\n\nNew business coming to Davenport's former Bed Bath & Beyond Deere held employee meeting Wednesday, no word yet on potential layoffs for Quad-Cities Two injured in shooting at NorthPark Mall in Davenport Monday Witnesses describe gunfire at NorthPark Mall that injured 2 Davenport code enforcement officer quits after argument with boss over Wold-owned duplex Quad-Cities business openings: New furniture store coming to Davenport, other happenings Teen arrested in relation to shooting at NorthPark Mall in Davenport Several Davenport teens accused of gang crimes; police report group violence down overall Second person dies after Friday house fire in Riverdale Arrowhead Ranch items up for online auction after facility's closure Northwest Bank acquired by Chicago-area bank Davenport developer pulls 16-unit central city development at Sixth and Sylvan One injured in Scott County motorcycle crash Iowa nursing home resident suffocated while trapped in bed rails, state says First Senior Bix sees strong turnout ahead of 50th Quad-City Times Bix 7\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nLove\n\n0\n\nFunny\n\n0\n\nWow\n\n0\n\nSad\n\n0\n\nAngry\n\n0\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news first game of the women's Olympic football tournament on Thursday.\n\nSpain are making their Olympic women's football debut at the Paris Games but are leading contenders to win the gold medal after their World Cup triumph in Australia and New Zealand last year.\n\nThey fell behind against Japan in the western French city of Nantes to Aoba Fujino's early free-kick, but Bonmati soon equalised before Mariona Caldentey netted the winner in the 74th minute.\n\nIt is the perfect start for Spain in Group C, in which rivals Nigeria and Brazil meet later.\n\nWith 12 teams split into three groups of four, there is margin for error as the two best third-placed teams will advance to the quarter-finals.\n\nThat will provide some comfort for Japan, who won the silver medal at London 2012.\n\nSpain's starting XI featured seven players who were in the line-up for last year's World Cup final win over England in Sydney, plus Alexia Putellas, the two-time former Ballon d'Or powerful for goalkeeper Cata Coll.\n\nHowever, Spain bossed possession and drew level midway through the first half when Bonmati was played in by Athenea del Castillo and rounded the goalkeeper to score.\n\nThey then grabbed what proved to be the winner when Caldentey came in from the left and played a quick exchange of passes with Bonmati before firing in.\n\nCanada shrug off spying Wednesday.\n\nHowever, Arsenal's Cloe Lacasse levelled in first-half stoppage time for Canada, who beat Sweden on penalties in the final in Tokyo three years ago.\n\nEvelyne Viens then latched onto a long ball forward to fire in the winner 11 minutes from the end.\n\nCanada's build-up had been overshadowed after an assistant coach and an analyst were sent home from the Olympics on the eve of their opening game.\n\nThe analyst, 43-year-old Joey Lombardi, was also given a suspended eight-month prison sentence for flying a drone over a New Zealand training session this week in Saint-Etienne.\n\nLombardi pleaded guilty when he appeared in court in Saint-Etienne on Wednesday.\n\nThe assistant coach was Jasmine Mander, to whom Lombardi reported.\n\nHead coach Bev Priestman apologised and decided to take no part in the game against New Zealand as a result because she felt it would not be appropriate.\n\nCanada and New Zealand are in Group A along with hosts France and She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward and former Stanford Star Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Bay FC's Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage. Kundananji signed with Bay FC on a record transfer fee of nearly $800,000 and has scored twice for the San Jose team this NWSL season.\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nBay FC forward Asisat Oshoala, the six-time African women's player of the year, did not see the field for Nigeria.\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long-range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\n___\n\nAP Soccer Writer James Robson, in Marseille, France, contributed to this report.", "source": {"uri": "mercurynews.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "San Jose Mercury News"}, She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nPeople are also reading...\n\nNorthwoods Falls closes in St. John, owners hope temporarily Davich: Frankly, this is the best hot dog joint in the Region Mascot Hall of Fame to close in September, 'going out with confetti' UPDATE: Valpo man identified as motorcyclist killed when SUV reportedly made sudden U-turn Valpo jewelry store burglarized; holes cut in wall, cops say Valparaiso tornado confirmed as county calls state in for help Former Lake County councilman could avoid jail time yet again in 3rd domestic battery case Crown Point man led chase, soiled police vehicle, report says Portage officers injured during high-speed chase with bikers armed with AK-47, report says UPDATE: Cedar Lake woman killed in Monday's storm remembered as 'rock of the family' Region police release photo of wanted man NWI Business Ins and Outs: Royale with Cheese, Top of the Morning, Casa Blanca, Estella's Cantina, El Jimador, Jet's Pizza, Wingstop and Wing Snob opening Ex-Crown Point real estate agents indicted on charges of $5 million in COVID relief fraud after allegedly spending money on Porsche and country club Big Lots closing stores in Chicagoland and Indiana, warns it may close all stores Sunday night house fire draws out several departments\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nLove\n\n0\n\nFunny\n\n0\n\nWow\n\n0\n\nSad\n\n0\n\nAngry\n\n0\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her.
