{"uri": "8243745083", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "22:08:36", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T22:08:36Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T22:06:34Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7450980544090271, "url": "https://siouxcityjournal.com/swanson-usa-olympics-soccer-women-roundup/article_c50e6f7c-d91b-535f-bfd3-314fa6262504.html", "title": "US women off to strong start", "body": "ASSOCIATED PRESS\n\nNICE, France -- Mallory Swanson scored a pair of goals just moments apart in the first half and the United States opened the Olympics with a 3-0 victory Thursday night over Zambia, giving new coach Emma Hayes a win in her first major tournament with the team.\n\nTrinity Rodman also scored for the United States, which is looking to add a record fifth gold medal to its Olympic collection.\n\nZambia was hurt in the 33rd minute when Pauline Zulu was sent off with a red card and the team was limited to 10 players the rest of the way.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nPeople are also reading... Two dead following Sunday night two-vehicle accident in Sioux City's westside Woodbury County Court Report for July 22, 2024 Specialty dog boutique store, Urban Mutts, opens in Sioux City Jason's Frozen Treats open second dine-in ice cream parlor BNSF Railway wants to remove collapsed Big Sioux River train bridge One dead after early Saturday morning collision in Sioux City Sioux City substitute teachers to receive extra pay for outside of normal day work Iowa nursing home resident suffocated while trapped in bed rails, state says Marriage licenses for Woodbury County for July 23, 2024 River-Cade crowns 2024 Queen of the River and princesses in Sioux City ceremony UPDATED: Okoboji lakes fall below target for lifting boat speeding limits Sioux City man charged with sexually abusing minor Woman's body recovered from overturned Jeep in Sac County river State baseball: Scrapy dynamic duo sends Crusaders to state title game, down top seeded Wahlert Postmaster concerned about dogs in Ingleside Avenue area biting mail carriers\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nFrance 3, Colombia 2\n\nFrance built a 3-0 lead in the first half and held off Colombia in Lyon.\n\nMarie-Antoinette Katoto scored a pair of goals and Kenza Dali added another for the hosts in Group A.\n\nCatalina Usme converted on a penalty early in the second half for Colombia, which was returning to the Olympics after missing out on the Tokyo Games. Manuela Pavi helped close the gap further with another goal in the 64th.\n\n0 Comments Love 0 Funny 0 Wow 0 Sad 0 Angry 0\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! {"uri": "8243729521", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "21:48:59", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T21:48:59Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T21:48:25Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.729411780834198, "url": "https://pantagraph.com/swanson-usa-olympics-soccer-women-roundup/article_a5be73f8-c1df-5332-95fa-88b989174945.html", "title": "US women off to strong start", "body": "ASSOCIATED PRESS\n\nNICE, France -- Mallory Swanson scored a pair of goals just moments apart in the first half and the United States opened the Olympics with a 3-0 victory Thursday night over Zambia, giving new coach Emma Hayes a win in her first major tournament with the team.\n\nTrinity Rodman also scored for the United States, which is looking to add a record fifth gold medal to its Olympic collection.\n\nZambia was hurt in the 33rd minute when Pauline Zulu was sent off with a red card and the team was limited to 10 players the rest of the way.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nPeople are also reading... Bloomington teen rebuilds landscape of alma mater for Eagle Scout project Riverdale man gets 123 years for 2020 murder in Bloomington Man struck by gunfire early Saturday in north Normal Video: Springfield woman ducked, apologized before fatal police shooting McLean County Fair selects 2024 royalty Pritzker, Illinois leaders react to Biden leaving presidential race 'Shocked, horrified,' Illinois leaders condemn police killing of Sonya Massey Funerals today for July 23 Flick Fact: That J.D. Vance beard and its McLean County significance? U High senior Jeremy Coleman willing his way to volleyball future Normal police investigating shots fired Tuesday night Ronald & Wanda Coyne Update: Canton police say missing 2-year-old has been found alive McLean County Fair food vendors offer something for everyone \ud83c\udf2d Bloomington man detained, accused of sexually assaulting teen at knifepoint\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nLove 0 Funny 0 Wow 0 Sad 0 Angry 0\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign court on Wednesday. She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nPeople are also reading... U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! * I understand and agree that 3-0.\n\nSpain are making their Olympic women's football debut at the Paris Games but are leading contenders to win gold after their World Cup triumph in Australia and New Zealand last year.\n\nThey fell behind against Japan in Group C in the western French city of Nantes to Aoba Fujino's superb early free-kick, but Bonmati soon equalised as she rounded the goalkeeper to score midway through the {"uri": "8243732886", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "21:53:55", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T21:53:55Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T21:53:10Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.686274528503418, "url": "https://napavalleyregister.com/swanson-usa-olympics-soccer-women-roundup/article_cdb6577b-9460-5ed4-affc-b15d4176007c.html", "title": "US women off to strong start", "body": "ASSOCIATED PRESS\n\nNICE, France -- Mallory Swanson scored a pair of goals just moments apart in the first half and the United States opened the Olympics with a 3-0 victory Thursday night over Zambia, giving new coach Emma Hayes a win in her first major tournament with the team.\n\nTrinity Rodman also scored for the United States, which is looking to add a record fifth gold medal to its Olympic collection.\n\nZambia was hurt in the 33rd minute when Pauline Zulu was sent off with a red card and the team was limited to 10 players the rest of the way.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nPeople are also reading... Update: Distillery building damaged by fire after Highway 29 crash in Napa Report: Visit Napa Valley staff allege toxic comments, secrecy by CEO Gallagher Vallejo man dies, Napan hurt in Highway 29 crash Restaurant owners, workers urge action against unpermitted food vending in Napa Growing pains: Violence-related NVUSD suspensions track with enrollment in middle schools Ira C. Smith, KVON/KVYN radio sports director since 1976, dies at age 88 Napa Valley Distillery plans to rebuild, reopen after fiery crash Vintage Wine Estates files for bankruptcy, sells Cosentino Winery in Napa Valley Napa County education trustee Ann Cash resigns after Mayacamas school approval Kevin Courtney, Napa Journal: My street is getting a major luxury upgrade CHP: K-9 sniffs out 70 pounds of meth during Napa traffic stop Update: Ridge Fire in Lake County is 15% contained; evacuation orders in effect Drivers to soon get a taste of Napa's Soscol Junction roundabouts Update: Highway 128 reopens in Napa County after submerged vehicle found Letter: Stop tainting the name of Alta Heights\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nPeople are also reading... U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\n0 Comments Love 0 Funny 0 Wow 0 Sad 0 Angry 0\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\n___\n\nAP Soccer Writer James Robson, in Marseille, France, contributed to this report.", "source": {"uri": four-time gold medallists the United States beat Zambia 3-0.\n\nSpain are making their Olympic women's football debut at the Paris Games but are leading contenders to win gold after their World Cup {"uri": "8243723685", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "21:41:43", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T21:41:43Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T21:40:46Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6666666865348816, "url": "https://heraldcourier.com/swanson-usa-olympics-soccer-women-roundup/article_12711dec-977a-596a-b985-a3beb2f56c0e.html", "title": "US women off to strong start", "body": "ASSOCIATED PRESS\n\nNICE, France -- Mallory Swanson scored a pair of goals just moments apart in the first half and the United States opened the Olympics with a 3-0 victory Thursday night over Zambia, giving new coach Emma Hayes a win in her first major tournament with the team.\n\nTrinity Rodman also scored for the United States, which is looking to add a record fifth gold medal to its Olympic collection.\n\nZambia was hurt in the 33rd minute when Pauline Zulu was sent off with a red card and the team was limited to 10 players the rest of the way.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her Olympic roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nPeople are also reading... National Ice Cream Day 2024: Get cool deals and freebies at Dairy Queen, Cold Stone and more HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: All Wolves now playing at West Ridge Bristol Casino records solid $14.35M month during June Kilgore remembered as \"larger than life\" trailblazer Housing complex rehab in Saltville wins $2.4 million state loan Campus keeps tradition strong Only the name has changed; 'The Classic' expected to become bigger and better This theater season brings friendship, camaraderie and nostalgia to the stage Owens will be missed at annual Creeper Trail Ride to End Cancer Herald Courier receives awards from Tennessee Press Association BRIEFS: VHSL to hold public forum at Abingdon on Wednesday; Top-15 finish for Adam Hooker (Lebanon) at State Open of Virginia HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Next man up part of high school football PREP SPORTS: VHSL leaders hold public meeting in Abingdon PREP FOOTBALL: Marquee games await Northeast Tennessee teams HIGH SCHOOL FOOTBALL: Versatile Elliott to see plenty of the field for Vikings\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game with what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on Hayes' Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario wasn't able to play in France because of minor knee irritation.\n\nIt was the first time the United States has faced Zambia on the international stage.\n\nWhile Zambia started stars Barbra Banda and Racheal Kundananji, neither of them was able to break through.\n\nBanda is a proven scorer, with 12 goals in 12 games this season for the Orlando Pride in the National Women's Soccer League. At the Tokyo Games, Banda had a pair of back-to-back hat tricks in the group stage.\n\nCanada 2, New Zealand 1\n\nEvelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at the Ferns' practice.\n\nViens, who came into the match as a substitute in the 67th, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post 12 minutes after entering.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead with a goal in the 13th minute, but Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start when two Canada staffers were sent home early for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand's practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without coach Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for the match to show accountability. However, she was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\nFIFA has opened a disciplinary inquiry into the matter, and Canadian Soccer launched an independent review.\n\nThe drone scandal marred the tournament's start. Canada won bronze medals in both the 2012 and 2016 Olympics before winning a gold in Tokyo.\n\nSpain 2, Japan 1\n\nWorld champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th.\n\nSpain might have had flashbacks to its 4-0 loss to Japan at last year's World Cup, but Bonmati -- who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months -- leveled the game nine minutes later when rounding goalkeeper Ayaka Yamashita.\n\nShe provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nGermany 3, Australia 0\n\nAfter its humbling group-stage exit from the Women's World Cup last year, Germany got off to a flying start at the Olympics by beating Australia in Marseille.\n\nMarina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corners in either half and Jule Brand fired in a third for the No. 4-ranked Germans from close range.\n\nWorld Cup semifinalist Australia lacked firepower without talismanic striker Sam Kerr, who is recovering from ACL damage.\n\nHegering's far post header gave Germany the lead in the 24th and Schueller rose highest to convert a second in the 64th.\n\nBrand had a simple finish from close range after Sarai Linder's low cross to the far post in the 68th.\n\nBrazil 1, Nigeria 0\n\nGabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute and Brazil went on to defeat Nigeria in Group C in Bordeaux.\n\nMarta, a six-time world player of the year, started for Brazil in her sixth Olympics. The 38-year-old captain has said this will be her last major tournament with the national team.\n\nBrazil's players were looking to send Marta off with a title in a major championship, something that has eluded her. Brazil has never won a gold medal in the Olympics but claimed silver in 2004 and 2008.\n\nBe the first to know\n\nGet local news delivered to your inbox!\n\nSign up! * I understand and agree that "USA, World Cup holders Spain win women's Olympic football openers", "body": "Canada shrugged off a spying scandal to beat New Zealand in their opening game at the Olympics\n\nReigning Ballon d'Or Aitana Bonmati scored one goal and helped create another as World Cup holders Spain beat Japan 2-1 in their first game of the women's Olympic football tournament on Thursday, while record four-time gold medallists the United States beat Zambia 3-0.\n\nSpain are making their Olympic women's football debut at the Paris Games but are leading contenders to win gold after their World Cup triumph in Australia and New Zealand last year.\n\nThey fell behind against Japan in Group C in the western French city of Nantes to Aoba Fujino's superb early free-kick, but Bonmati soon equalised as she rounded the goalkeeper to score midway through the first half.\n\nSpain then grabbed the winner in the 74th minute when Mariona Caldentey exchanged passes with Bonmati before firing in.\n\nWith 12 teams split into three groups of four, there is margin for error as the two best third-placed sides will advance to the quarter-finals.\n\nThat will provide some comfort for Japan, silver medallists at London 2012.\n\nA strong Spain starting XI featured seven players who were in the line-up for last year's World Cup final win over England in Sydney, plus Alexia Putellas, the two-time former Ballon d'Or winner.\n\nIn the same section, two-time silver medallists Brazil beat Nigeria 1-0 in Bordeaux.\n\nFormer world player of the year Marta, in her sixth Olympics at the age of 38, had an effort disallowed for offside before setting up Gabi Nunes for the only goal late in the first half.\n\n- Swanson double -\n\nThe USA have come to the Games with a young squad but with high hopes of success under new coach Emma Hayes.\n\nThey were comfortable winners against Zambia in Nice but should have triumphed by a greater margin after netting three times in the first half against opponents who had a player sent off before the break.\n\nTrinity Rodman and Mallory Swanson both hit the woodwork before Rodman -- daughter of former NBA superstar Dennis Rodman -- scored on 17 minutes with a lovely turn and finish in the box.\n\nSwanson made it 2-0 on 24 minutes when she controlled Lindsey Horan's pass and finished, and she netted again just a minute later, this time rounding the goalkeeper to slot in.\n\nZambia's Pauline Zulu was left in tears as she was sent off following a VAR review shortly before the break for a foul on Sophia Smith. However, the USA could not add any more goals with the extra player.\n\nMore from this section BBC to axe 500 more jobs in bid to be 'more agile' Sex Differences in Knee Arthritis Emerge as Early as Childhood Trump attack gunman searched online about JFK shooting: FBI chief\n\nAlso in Group B, 2016 gold medallists Germany outclassed Australia, winning 3-0 in Marseille with Marina Hegering and Lea Schueller both scoring headers before Jule Brand wrapped up the victory.\n\nThe USA and Germany meet each other in Marseille on Sunday.\n\n- Canada shrug off spying scandal -\n\nFrance survived a wobble to beat Colombia 3-2 in Lyon, where there were plenty of empty seats to greet the host nation.\n\nMarie-Antoinette Katoto scored twice in the first half either side of a Kenza Dali strike as France appeared to be cruising.\n\nHowever, Catalina Usme pulled one back from a penalty early in the second half and substitute Manuela Pavi further reduced the deficit before a red card for Mayra Ramirez ended Colombian hopes of snatching a point.\n\nIn the same Group A, reigning Olympic champions Canada shrugged off a spying scandal to claim a 2-1 win over New Zealand in Saint-Etienne.\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the lead before a sparse crowd at the Stade Geoffroy-Guichard.\n\nArsenal's Cloe Lacasse levelled in first-half stoppage time for Canada, who beat Sweden on penalties in the final in Tokyo three years ago. Evelyne Viens then fired in the winner 11 minutes from time.\n\nCanada's build-up had been overshadowed after an assistant coach and an analyst were sent home from the Olympics on the eve of the game.\n\nThe analyst, 43-year-old Joey Lombardi, was also given a suspended eight-month prison sentence for flying a drone over a New Zealand training session this week in Saint-Etienne.\n\nHead coach Bev Priestman apologised and took no part in the game against New Zealand, feeling it would not be appropriate.\n\n\"As a Canadian, these are not our values. Julio Cortez/Asssociated Press\n\nNICE, France -- Mallory Swanson scored a pair of goals just moments apart in the first half and the United States opened the Olympics with a 3-0 victory over Zambia on Thursday night, giving new coach Emma Hayes a win in her first major tournament with the team.\n\nTrinity Rodman also scored for the United States, which is looking to add a record fifth gold medal to its Olympic collection.\n\nZambia was hurt in the 33rd minute when Pauline Zulu was sent off with a red card and the team was limited to 10 players the rest of the way. Zulu sobbed as she left the field.\n\nHayes took over the U.S. team in late May after finishing out the season with Chelsea in the Women's Super League. She shook things up a bit with her roster, leaving star forward Alex Morgan, a veteran of three Olympics, at home.\n\nHayes is charged with leading the Americans as they seek to distance themselves from the disappointment of last summer's Women's World Cup, when they crashed out in the round of 16.\n\nRodman, making her Olympic debut, scored in the 17th minute. U.S. captain Lindsey Horan passed to Rodman, who deftly shot around onrushing Zambian goalkeeper Ngambo Musole.\n\nAdvertisement\n\nSwanson scored twice within 70 seconds in the 24th and 25th minutes to give the Americans a 3-0 lead in the Group B match in Nice.\n\nU.S. forward Sophia Smith left the game because of what appeared to be an ankle injury late in the first half and was replaced by Lynn Williams.\n\nWilliams was originally an alternate on the Olympic roster, but Catarina Macario isn't able to play in France because of a knee injury.\n\nIn other games:\n\n* Evelyne Viens scored in the 79th minute to give reigning Olympic champion Canada a 2-1 victory over New Zealand in a match that was overshadowed by allegations of drone surveillance at New Zealand practices.\n\nViens, who entered as a substitute in the 67th minute, took a long pass from Jessie Fleming and tucked it into the goal at the opposite post.\n\nAdvertisement\n\nMackenzie Barry gave New Zealand the early lead in the 13th minute. Cloe Lacasse equalized for Canada in first-half stoppage time.\n\nThe Group A match in Saint-Etienne was controversial before the start. Two Canada staffers were sent home for their alleged involvement with drones that were reported over a pair of New Zealand practices.\n\nCanada played the opener without its head coach, Bev Priestman, who stepped away from the team for one match. She was adamant at practice Wednesday that she had no knowledge of the drone use.\n\n* World champion Spain came from behind to beat Japan in Group C, thanks to a goal and an assist from Ballon d'Or winner Aitana Bonmati.\n\nPlaying in its first Olympics, Spain fell behind at La Beaujoire Stadium in Nantes after Aoba Fumino's brilliant long range free kick flew into the top corner in the 13th minute.\n\nBonmati, who has dominated the individual awards in women's soccer over the past 12 months, leveled the game nine minutes later, then provided the assist for Mariona Caldentey to score the winner in the 74th with a curling shot into the bottom corner.\n\nAdvertisement\n\n* Marina Hegering and Lea Schueller scored headers from corner kicks, and Jule Brand fired in a third goal for fourth-ranked Germany in a 3-0 win over Australia in Marseille.\n\n* Gabi Nunes scored in the 37th minute as Brazil defeated Nigeria, 1-0, in Bordeaux.\n\n* Marie-Antoinette Katoto scored a pair of goals and Kenza Dali added another as France built a 3-0 lead in the first half and held on for a 3-2 win over Colombia in Lyon.\n\nTENNIS: Rafael Nadal and Novak Djokovic could meet in the second round of the men's singles tournament - which might end up being the last event of Nadal's career.\n\nDjokovic was drawn Thursday against Australian Matthew Ebden in the first round, and Nadal faces Hungarian Marton Fucsovics, with the winners of those matches meeting next. The tennis competition begins Saturday at Roland Garros.\n\nTop-ranked Iga Swiatek of Poland faces Irina-Camelia Begu of Romania in the first round of the women's draw, with second-seeded American Coco Gauff taking on Australian Ajla Tomljanovi\u0107.\n\nAdvertisement\n\nFour-time major winner Naomi Osaka of Japan will play three-time major champion Angelique Kerber of Germany. Kerber, 36, announced Thursday's that she'll retire after the Olympics.\n\n* Two-time men's singles gold medalist Andy Murray pulled out of the singles tournament before Thursday's draw and only will compete in doubles with Dan Evans.\n\nMurray, a 37-year-old from Britain, has said these Olympics will be the final event of his career.\n\nFIGURE SKATING: The U.S. figure skating team was formally
